                registration of real estate rights, local government bodies and other bodies that
                may have the said information, as well as from the alleged owners of the land and

404.    To address resettlement and livelihood restoration issues, an Inter Agency Commission
on Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement (IALRAR) at district level will be established by an Order
of the Head of the Local Administration. The Commission will include representatives from:
              -    local state administration,
              -    executive and representative bodies of local self-government,
              -    construction and urban development authorities,
              -    real estate registration authorities,
              -    land supervision authorities,
              -    local agricultural development departments.
405. The Commission may, if necessary, invite representatives of relevant government agencies.
Representatives of the public may also be included on the Commission.

       a) Conduct a screening of land parcels (pastures and adjacent areas) required for the Project,

            -     legal status and any restrictions on use,
            -     presence of registered rights or encumbrances.

        b) Conduct a preliminary cadastral survey, documenting:
           -   parcel boundaries and shares of common use,
           -   the presence of real estate and utility infrastructure,
           -   and other relevant cadastral data.

        c) Provide support for the Grievance Redress Mechanism
           -     Provide support to local agencies (districts) on land related issues



10.2 Local Level
10.2.1 Local government administrations of Toktogul , Toguz-Toro and Zhumgal districts
407.     The local state administration in the district is responsible for the following tasks:
    a. Provides information and assists in identifying persons, lands and other assets subject
       to acquisition;
    b. Establishment of district-level livestock routes, including livestock stopping areas;
    c. Resolving issues related to the provision of pastures in accordance with administrative
       procedures;
    d. Assists in organizing and participating in the census and inventory of losses survey of
       lands and other assets;
    e. Assists persons whose lands and assets are acquired in resolving issues arising as a
       result of forced resettlement;
    f. Assists in organizing and holding public meetings and consultations

10.2.2 Aiyl Okmotu of Sary-Kamysh, Toluk, E. Imanaliev, and Atai Aiyl Aimaks
408.   The executive power of local government bodies includes the following tasks:
    a. Organization of work on the management and use of state pastures for pasture users
       in the project area;
    b. Provision of pastures for urgent (temporary) use in the project area

10.2.3 District level cadastral unit Toktogul, Toguz- Toro district branches of the State
      Agency of Land Resources, Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography
409.      These agencies will be responsible for the following tasks.
       a. Provide information on registration of rights on land;
       b. Provide information on restrictions on land;
       c. Information on cadastral maps;
       d. Provide copies legal titles (red/ blue book);
       e. Conducting state registration of rights to land and other assets;
       f. Registration and issuance of documents certifying rights to a land plot, based on title
           documents;
       g. Provide land plots in kind (on the ground) and establish and secure the boundaries of
           land use of legal entities and individuals;

       h. Carry on the implementation of land management, topographic and cadastral surveys

       Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal Services under the Cabinet

       a. Provide information on pasture management

          the placement of pasture users, cattle routes and other pasture infrastructure).
10.2.6 Pastures Committee/Municipal Enterprises
412.     These bodies will have the following tasks;
       a. Identify pasture users for inclusion in the list of persons whose pastures are subject
          to acquisition ;
       b. Participate in and facilitate consultations and information campaigns among pasture
          users;
       c. Issue pasture tickets/contracts for the right to use pastures in the territory to which
          they were resettled;
       d. Resolve disputes among pasture users;

10.3 Third-Party Monitors
413.   It is required to hire an agency/ organization or research institute specializing in social
sciences for each project province, to conduct socio-economic surveys, periodically monitor and
evaluate the implementation of the LRRPs.
414.   K1-PMO will sign contract with each third-party monitors. Third-party monitors will
report periodically on progress made and make recommendations for resolving the problems
detected in the monitoring process.

11 CONSULTATION, PARTICIPATION AND DISCLOSURE

11.1 Objectives of Public Consultation
415.   The main objective of the consultation process is to carry out meaningful dialogue with
the aim to avoid potential for conflicts, address the concerns of displaced persons to the extent
possible, avoid bottlenecks to minimize project delays and contribute towards mitigating
adverse impacts from involuntary resettlement. The consultation with the displaced persons
serves as the conduit for education, information dissemination and exchange about the project.
416.    This process should be consistent with the objectives set out in the project’s Stakeholder
Engagement Plan (SEP). As per the SEP, consultations should ensure that women’s perspectives,
as well as those of vulnerable groups, are obtained and their interests factored into all aspects
of resettlement planning and implementation.
417.    Information dissemination to PAPs and involved agencies is an important part of Project
preparation and implementation. Consultation with PAPs and ensuring their active participation
will reduce the potential for conflicts and minimize the risk of Project delays. This will also
enable the Project to design the Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement program as a
comprehensive development program to suit the needs and priorities of the PAPs, thereby
maximizing the economic and social benefits of investments.
418.     Carrying out meaningful consultations for the K1-HPP project requires:
    -    Beginning early in the project planning process to gather initial views on the project
         proposal and inform project design;
    -    Encouraging affected and interested stakeholder feedback, particularly as a way of
         informing project design and engagement by stakeholders in the identification and
         mitigation of environmental and social risks and impacts;
    -    Continuing the stakeholder engagement process on an ongoing basis, as risks and
         impacts arise;
    -    Is based on the prior disclosure and dissemination of relevant, transparent, objective,
         meaningful and easily accessible information in a timeframe that enables meaningful
         consultations with stakeholders in a culturally appropriate format, in relevant local
         language(s) and is understandable to stakeholders;
    -    Project GRM accessibility, availability and efficiency;
    -    Considering and responding to feedback;
    -    Supporting active and inclusive engagement with project-affected parties;
    -    Is free from of external manipulation, interference, coercion, discrimination, and
         intimidation; and
    -    Is documented and disclosed by the Borrower. Ensuring that the meeting minutes are
         thorough and include all essential elements. It is important to document all
         stakeholders' questions to capture and address their concerns effectively.




                                                                                                                    110


                                                                                                                   Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement
Framework

11.2 Stakeholders
11.2.1 Categories of Stakeholders
419.   ESS10 identifies two broad categories of stakeholders: "project affected parties" and
"other interested parties". ESS10 also indicates that the Borrower will identify those project-
affected parties (individuals or groups) who, because of their particular circumstances, may be
disadvantaged or vulnerable.
420.   Project affected parties (PAPs) are individuals, groups and other parties in the project
area who are directly or indirectly, positively or negatively (actually or potentially) affected by
the project and/or who have been identified as the most susceptible to project-related changes
and who should be actively involved in identifying impacts and their significance, as well as in
deciding on mitigation and management measures.
421.    Other interested parties are individuals/groups/organizations who believe or feel that
their interests are affected by the project and/or who have the potential to affect the project
outcomes and its implementation process in some way.

11.2.2 Project Affected Parties
422.     Project affected parties for the K1-HPP include the following groups:
    -    Communities directly affected by the dam/reservoir through loss of
         land/pastures/assets and access to these land/pastures/assets;
    -    Land users affected by the loss of land/pastures/assets and access to these
         land/pastures/assets and loss of livelihoods
    -    Vulnerable groups (Low-income households and individuals; The elderly, people of pre-
         retirement age; People with disabilities; Women headed low income households).
11.2.3 Project Interested Parties
423.     Project affected parties for the K1-HPP include the following groups
    • Kyrgyz Government Ministries and Related Organizations
    -    Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic;
    -    Ministry of Finance of the Kyrgyz Republic;
    -    Ministry of Economy and Commerce of the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Ministry of Emergency Situations of the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Ministry of Water Resources, Agriculture and Processing Industry of the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    District departments of agricultural develop-ment of the Ministry
    -    Ministry of Labor and Social Security and Migration of the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Ministry of Natural Resources, Ecology and Technical Supervision of the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Jalal-Abad Regional Administration of the Ministry of Natural Resources, Ecology and
         Technical Supervision
    -    Ministry of Construction, Architecture and Housing and Communal Services of the
         Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Jalal-Abad regional administration in urban planning and architecture
    -    State Enterprise for Land Management " KyrgyzGiproZem " under the State Agency for
         Land Resources, Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography under the Cabinet of Ministers of
         the Kyrgyz Republic
    -    Ministry of Culture, Information, Sports and Youth of the KGZ Republic

11.2.4 Socially vulnerable populations
425.   It is particularly important to understand whether project impacts may
disproportionately affect socially vulnerable populations, who are often not in a position to
communicate their concerns or understand the impacts of the project. Vulnerable status may
be due to origin, gender, age, health status, economic difficulties, financial insecurity, socially
disadvantaged position in the community (e.g., unemployed youth), dependence on others
(dependency) or on natural resources, and etc.
426.    Interaction with vulnerable groups and individuals often requires special measures and
assistance to support their participation in the project-related decision making, so that their
awareness and contributions to the overall process are comparable with those of other
stakeholders. Socially vulnerable population groups under the project may include the following
categories, among others:

12 GRIEVANCE REDRESS MECHANISM

12.1 General Provisions
454.    This Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM) is created as a Project mechanism at the
local and national levels for the receipt, registration, consideration, assessment, resolution of
grievances and decision-making on them arising in the process of implementing the K1-HPP
Project, in accordance with the national legislation of the Kyrgyz Republic and the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
455.   This GRM is intended only for external stakeholders affected by the Project and not for
the Project employees and contractors involved in the implementation of the Project. A
separate internal GRM for the Project workers’ grievances will be created for use by Project
employees and contractors.
456.     Appeals in the form of obtaining information, recommendations, requests from citizens
for assistance in the implementation and restoration of their constitutional rights and freedoms
or constitutional rights and freedoms of other persons, or a message about the violation of laws
and other regulatory legal acts, as well as about shortcomings in the activities of state bodies
and local government bodies and their officials not related to the implementation of
administrative procedures, are considered taking into account the Law of the Kyrgyz Republic
“On the procedure for considering citizens' appeals” dated May 4, 2007 No. 67 and the WB
ESS10 “Stakeholder Engagement and Information Disclosure” requirements.
457.     A detailed GRM will be developed and approved by the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz
Republic (MoE) after approval of the K1- HPP project and must fully comply with the provisions
specified in this GRM.
458.    Grievances related to land acquisition, land use restrictions and involuntary
resettlement, livelihood impacts, unfair compensation, inadequacy of rights, inaccuracies in
detailed measurements, or problems with the donation process, etc., will be addressed taking
into account the GRM details given in the LRRF.
12.2 Principles
459.   This GRM is based on following fundamental principles for handling grievances and
guarantees:
         -    Accessibility: GRM should be easily accessible to all external interested parties,
              taking into account confidentiality, legal obligations and vulnerability separate
              persons.
         -    Efficiency and effectiveness: necessary handle grievances effectively , promptly,
              discretely, objectively, sensitively, responsibly and transparent.
         -    Communication: Provide applicants with timely and continuous information on the
              progress of the review grievances , including reasons for any delays.
         -    Impartiality: Those responsible for handling grievances should not have no basis
              for favouring one solution over another or one party over another, and no
              outsiders should be allowed to interfere with the complaint resolution process .
         -    No costs: grievances should be resolved free of charge to the party that initiated
              the problem or concern.



                                                                                                                    124


                                                                                                                   Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement
Framework

         -    No restrictions on civil or legal rights: the mandatory consideration of anonymous
              grievances, participation in the MRI should not hinder or complicate the victim's
              right to other judicial, administrative, civil or other means of legal protection not
              prohibited by the legislation of the Kyrgyz Republic .
         -    Confidentiality: All grievances must be treated confidentially throughout the
              process and no information must be given to anyone not involved in the
              complaint.
         -    Anonymous and confidential grievances are also subject to consideration. The
              project encourages the submission of grievances through various channels,
              including anonymous submissions, at different levels.
         -    The fundamental rights and interests of PAPs must be considered and protected
              with special attention;
         -    Application of traditional cultural mechanisms: filing and resolving grievances and
              conflict issues , taking into account established effective mechanisms based on
              traditional culture and customs.
7.3. GRM procedure
460.     The GRM shall include the following:
         -    Various ways for applicants to file grievances, including filling grievances:
              anonymously, in person or through a representative , by telephone, by text
              message, by mail, by email or through a website;
         -    Maintaining a record of grievances , which are recorded in writing and maintained
              as a database (Grievance Log);
         -    Publicly announced procedures setting out the manner and timeframe within
              which complainants may expect acknowledgement, response and resolution of
              their grievances;
         -    An appeals process (including the national court system) to which unresolved
              grievances may be referred if resolution of the complaint has not been reached.

7.3.1. GRM Levels

461.    The grievance redress mechanism is an integral part of the institutional arrangement in
relation to the environmental and social risk management. A two-stage process will be
established for the Project as described below. Table 12 and Figure 3 summarize this process.
462.   The complainant will be provided with assistance in relation to the grievances handling
process at all levels of consideration. Complainants have the right to ask any questions, express
concerns or complain to local government officials, state authorities or Project staff.
463.    First level, Local. At the village level (Aiyl Okmotu/, District Land Commission), local
contact persons of Aiyl Okmotu receive/register grievances from applicants in the Grievance
Registration Log), inform the K1-PMO and responds within the competence of Aiyl Okmotu. If
the grievance (request/issue) cannot be addressed by the Aiyl Okmotu within their
competence, the complaint is escalated to the K1-PMO.
464.   For land and other District level issues, K1-PMO will involve the district state
administration including the Land Commission if grievance is related to land issues.



                                                                                                                    125


                                                                                                                   Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement
Framework

465.     In the event that the applicant is not satisfied and/or the issue cannot be resolved at the
first level, the complaint is sent to the second (central) level.
466.    Second level, Central. At the second level, the K1-PMO responsible staff receives and
registers the complaint and forwards it to the K1-PMO director. The K1-PMO director assigns
the K1-PMO staff responsible for resolution of the complaint, further together with other
relevant staff, they will review the compliant and make a decision. Complaints requiring a
collegial decision are reviewed by a GRM committee established by the MoE.
467.  For grievances on the first and second level in the form of obtaining information,
recommendations, requests from citizens not related to the implementation of administrative
procedures, a decision is made within 14 working days,
468.   If on the first and second level, special checks, additional materials or other measures
are required to resolve a complaint, the resolution period may be extended: it can be prolonged
exceptionally for no longer than 30 calendar days.
469.   For grievances on the first and second level in the form of obtaining information,
recommendations, requests from citizens not related to the implementation of administrative
procedures, a decision is made within 14 working days, and for grievances directed at the
actions or inactions of state and municipal bodies that have entailed legal and /or factual
consequences for individuals or legal entities, a decision is made within 30 days.
470.    If on the first and second level, special checks, additional materials or other measures
are required to resolve a complaint, the resolution period may be extended: it can be prolonged
exceptionally for no longer than 30 calendar days. for the complaints not related to the
implementation of administrative procedures and no longer 60 calendar days for the
complaints directed at the actions or inactions of state and municipal bodies that have entailed
legal and /or factual consequences for individuals or legal entities.
471.   The GRM should not interfere with or hinder the applicant’s right to other legal
remedies. The applicant may terminate participation in the project GRM process at any time
and seek resolution through the courts in accordance with the legislation of the Kyrgyz
Republic.
472.    Grievances directed at the actions or inactions of state and municipal bodies that have
resulted in legal and /or actual consequences for individuals or legal entities as a result of the
implementation of the Project shall be considered taking into account the Law of the Kyrgyz
Republic “On the Fundamentals of Administrative Activity and Administrative Procedure”
(dated July 31, 2015, No. 210) and the WB ESS10 “Stakeholder Engagement and Information
Disclosure” requirements. This Law applies to actions and inactions of administrative bodies
that have caused actual consequences for individuals and regulates the procedure for appealing
administrative acts. An administrative complaint must be submitted within 30 working days. If
there is a valid reason for missing the deadline, the period may be restored, a request must be
submitted within 30 working days from the date the reason for the delay no longer applies.




                                                                                                                    126


                                                                                                                   Official Use Only

within the territory of the Aiyl Okmotu, in locations that are convenient and visible to the

12.2.3 Grievance recording and database
476.    All received grievances, including requests, proposals, complaints, are subject to
registration in the Grievances Log which is maintained both in electronic and paper format. The
LFPs at local level and the K1-PMO focal point at central level register received grievances,
providing detailed information such as the date of registration, applicant's information and
contact details, the essence and reasons for the appeal, and the category of the grievance.
477.    All the above-mentioned LFPs at local level and the PMO responsible staff (for GRM
registration, coordination and monitoring) at central level have access to the Grievance Log to
register and monitor the timeframes for reviewing grievances. If necessary, they can enter
additional information to extend the timeframes for reviewing grievances and appeals,
provided there is a justification for the extension and inform the Applicant in case of
prolongation.
12.3 Handling SEA/SH grievances
478.  All World Bank-financed projects must comply with the WB ESF requirements on the
prevention of Sexual Exploitation and Abuse/Sexual Harassment (SEA/SH) and implement
measures to raise awareness and mitigate the risks of SEA/SH.
479.    The Project will develop a clear and transparent GRM process for receiving,
investigating, and resolving SEA/SH grievances. The GRM will ensure access and confidentiality
for the consideration of special grievances, allowing complainants to voice their concerns
without fear of retaliation. These grievances will be investigated promptly, and all responsible
parties will be held accountable.
480.   The K1-PMO will appoint SEA/SH focal points within the PMO and among contractors to
oversee the implementation of SEA/SH prevention measures and handle grievances.
481.     The Project will use additional mitigation measures proportionate to the risk:
         -    Establish a secure and confidential reporting system for SEA/SH grievances,
              accessible to all community members.
         -    Conduct regular training sessions for project staff, contractors, and community
              members on SEA/SH prevention, reporting procedures, and the importance of
              confidentiality.
         -    Disseminate information about SEA/SH risks, prevention measures, and available
              support services through community meetings, posters, and leaflets.
         -    Ensure that all data related to SEA/SH grievances are securely stored and only
              accessible to authorized personnel.
         -    Establish a process for the prompt and impartial investigation of SEA/SH
              grievances.
         -    Establish partnerships with local organizations and service providers to offer
              comprehensive support to survivors.
         -    Regularly monitor the implementation of SEA/SH prevention measures and the
              effectiveness of the GRM.
         -    Include SEA/SH-related data and analysis in project progress reports to ensure
              transparency and accountability.




                                                                                                                    130


                                                                                                                   Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP: Sustainable and Transformational Energy Program   Draft Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement
Framework

12.4 Monitoring and reporting
482.    The K1-PMO will establish a system to monitor the grievance management and
satisfaction of complainants. This will involve regular follow-ups with complainants to assess
their satisfaction with the grievance resolution process and the outcomes. The K1-PMO will
conduct periodic surveys and feedback sessions to gather insights on the effectiveness and
fairness of the grievance redress mechanism. The feedback collected will be analyzed to identify
areas for improvement and ensure that the grievance redress process is responsive to the needs
and concerns of the community.
483.     The K1-PMO will also ensure that all feedback is documented and used to enhance the
overall effectiveness of the grievance management system. The K1-PMO responsible staff
(Social Specialist and M&E Specialist) will monitor the timeframes for reviewing grievances at
all levels. If additional investigations are needed, including the involvement of third parties, the
review timeframes may be reasonably extended. If there is a justified need and the deadlines
for considering grievances and appeals are extended, the PMO staff assigned to the specific
grievance will prepare summary information and make appropriate notes in the unified GRM
Log.
484.   The K1-PMO shall prepare and submit a monthly report on grievances to the MoE. The
report shall include the number of grievances at both the local and central levels, along with
the number of grievances resolved and ongoing, categorized by GRM categories and levels.
Additionally, the PMO shall prepare and submit quarterly reports for review by the Bank as part
of the E&S risk management performance reports. The overall effectiveness of the grievance
management procedure will be assessed semi-annually by the project management.
12.5 World Bank Redress Grievances Services
485.   Communities and individuals who believe they have been affected by a World Bank-
supported project can submit complaints using the existing project-level grievance redress
mechanisms or the World Bank Grievance Redress Service (GRS). The GRS ensures that
grievances received are dealt with in a timely manner to resolve any project-related issues.
Affected communities and individuals may submit a complaint to the World Bank's Independent
Inspection Panel, which is to determine whether any harm has occurred resulting from the
World Bank's non-compliance with its policies and procedures.
486.    Complaints may be submitted at any time after concerns have been brought to the
attention of the World Bank and the management has had an opportunity to respond. For
information on how to submit a complaint to the World Bank's corporate Grievance Redress
Service (GRS), visit http://www.worldbank.org/en/projects-operations/products-and-
services/grievance-redressservice. For information on how to submit a complaint to the World
Bank’s Inspection Panel, visit: www.inspectionpanel.org
487.  Complaints can also be submitted at the World Bank office in Bishkek. Contact details of
the World Bank office in the Kyrgyz Republic is as follows:
         St. Abdrakhmanova, 191, Bishkek, 720011
         Bishkek Hyatt Regency, 2nd floor
         Tel : (996-312) 625-262

13 BUDGET

13.1 Funding for Livelihood Restoration and Resettlement
488.    The full cost of resettlement will be considered as a part of overall project costs,
including adequate contingency to cover unexpected circumstances or cost increases. This
includes, but is not limited to:
    -    Compensation at replacement cost for loss of immovable assets;
    -    Cost of transport of all movable assets to new sites;
    -    Compensation for lost crops, fruit trees or other produce;
    -    Transitional assistance including targeted assistance for vulnerable persons;
    -    Cost of livelihood restoration measures,
    -    Costs for restoration of access
    -    Costs for independent monitoring
489.     The details of LRRP implementation budget, and source of funding for all resettlement
activities will be disclosed in each LRRP, which will include an itemized budget for all individual
activities, staff time and training, provisions for inflation and monitoring costs.
13.2 Estimated Budget
490.   The budget for compensation of lost assets, LRRP and restoration of access is estimated
at USD 5,215,820. It includes the following items:
491.  Costs for compensation for lost assets and allowances (reservoir area and SPZ): USD
492,673
   - Costs for Livelihood Restoration Plan implementation: USD 1,868,981.
492. Costs for restoration of access: USD 2,000,000
493. Costs for independent monitoring: USD 50,000
494. Costs for preparation of 2 LRRPs: USD 330,000
495. Contingency costs (10%): USD 474,165
496.   This budget remains preliminary and will have to be revised and updated during LRRP2
preparation once all the census and IOL will be completed.

14 MONITORING AND REPORTING
497.   Monitoring of implementation is a continuous process during project implementation. It
provides concerned agencies with updated information on the Project's status. It will determine the
Project's actual progress, its likelihood of success, and any difficulties arising, and facilitate
adjustments to implementation of the Project implementation as soon as possible. It consists of
internal and external monitoring.
14.1 Internal Monitoring
498.   Internal monitoring of the LRRPs implementation is the main responsibility of the K1-PMO
with the support of the project consultants, which will be regularly implemented through progress
reports made by the K1-PMO. The findings will be recorded in quarterly reports before being
submitted to the MoE and WB. Internal monitoring reports will include the following information:
 (i)     Number of PAHs according to different impact types, condition of the compensation
         reimbursement, relocation and income recovery of the PAHs;
 (ii)    Finance allocation to the activities or reimbursement of compensation and the reimbursed
         budget for each activity;
 (iii)   Final result on complaints redress and any remaining issue which require the administrative
         authorities of some levels to solve;
 (iv)    Arisen issues during the implementation stage;
 (v)     Implementation schedule of the updated actual resettlement.
499.     The internal monitoring indicators include but are not limited to the following issues:
                                  Table 53: Internal Monitoring Indicators

14.2 Third-party monitoring (Independent Monitoring)
500.    An independent agency will be hired by the K1-PMO to monitor the implementation of the
livelihood restoration and resettlement plans. The agency is called the Independent Monitoring
Agency (IMA). The independent agency can be a research institution/company, a non-governmental
organization or an independent consulting firm etc. The agency must have expertise in the social
sciences and considerable experience in independent monitoring of the implementation of
resettlement. The implementation of the independent monitoring mission should be based on the
terms of reference approved by WB. The independent monitoring agency will begin its work as soon
as the project implementation begins.
501.    The overall objective of independent monitoring is to provide a periodic independent
evaluation of the results of implementing the resettlement objectives, the changes in living
standards and employment, income rehabilitation and the social basis of those affected,
effectiveness, impacts and sustainability of citizen entitlements, the need for additional measures
to minimize the damage (if any), and identifying strategic lessons for making and planning policies
in the future.
502.    In addition to the evaluation of the information provided in the assessment report of the
internal monitoring unit, the Independent Monitoring consultant will also conduct sample testing
every 6 months. The sample size should be 50% of displaced households and affected households,
and at least 10% of the remaining households in each LRRP in order to:
 (i)     Determine whether or not the procedures for the participation of affected people, and
         procedures for compensation and rehabilitation for affected persons matches the policy
         framework and LRRPs.

  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                      Official Use Only    Page 137
                                                                                                of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


 (ii)    Ensure the process of project implementation, procedures for consultation and information
         dissemination, publicity and compensation policies are conducted and transparent.
 (iii)   Evaluate whether the objectives of the policy framework on improving or at least recovering
         the income and living standards of affected persons are being met.
 (iv)    A set of quantitative indicators of socio-economic impacts of the implementation of the
         project for those affected.
 (v)     Propose amendments, where required, during the process of implementing the
         resettlement action plan, in order to achieve the principles and objectives of the policy
         framework.
 (vi)    The level of satisfaction of affected persons on different aspects of the resettlement action
         plan will be monitored and recorded. The operation of the grievance redress mechanism and
         the time required to resolve a complaint may be monitored.
 (vii) During the process of implementation, trends in living standards are observed and
         investigated. Any potential problems in the restoration of living standards are reported.
 (viii) The Independent Monitoring Agency must submit a periodic report every 6 months,
         outlining the findings of the monitoring process. This monitoring report will be discussed
         with K1-PMO before submission to World Bank.
503.   The ToR for third-party monitoring will be prepared by the K1-PMO and submitted to the
Bank for approval.
14.3 Evaluation
504.    Evaluation will be carried out under the project in the form of an assessment at the specified
time on the impact of relocation and whether the objectives have been achieved. Independent
monitoring will make an assessment of the resettlement process and impacts within 6-12 months
of the completion of all resettlement activities.
505.      If through the evaluation, the affected households are found not to have recovered their
livelihood accordingly, and the objectives of the project have not been achieved, the affected
households will be supported with appropriate funding. The Independent Monitoring Report should
be sent to the K1-PMO and directly to the World Bank in order to monitor/supervise the progress
and effectiveness of compensation. The Bank will continue to conduct their surveillance until the
resettlement activities noted in the LRRP report have been implemented. Upon the completion of
the project, the implementation completion report (ICR) will evaluate the achievements of the
resettlement and the lessons to be drawn which will be incorporated into the evaluation of K1-PMO
. If this evaluation determines that the objectives of the resettlement work have not been achieved
as expected, the ICR will evaluate the suitability of future resettlement measures.
506.  The evaluation will be made on the basis of the socio-economic survey among affected
households, to be conducted at the end of the project (or the end of the sub-project).
Criteria which need to be considered and evaluated after the end of the project include:
 (i)     The policy of compensation, support and resettlement has been applied
 (ii)    The promulgation of information
 (iii)   The consultation of stakeholders
 (iv)    The implementation of compensation, support and resettlement

  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                   Official Use Only    Page 138
                                                                                             of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


 (v) The existing problems
 (vi) Standard of living and restoration of the lives of the affected people
 (vii) Implementation capacity
 (viii) Claims and claim settlement
 (ix) Compare entitlement policies between approved update LRRP and implementation in real
         terms in order to evaluate the degree of compliance degree and achieve the project policy
         objectives.
507.    To evaluate the performance of the entire LRRPs, a sample survey of the socio-economic
profile of PAHs and an assessment of the affected households and the post-assessment for the
project will be carried out in line with the above-mentioned criteria within 6 months to 1 year after
the completion of the activities of the LRRP. A selected sample survey of households will be taken
from the list of households in the baseline survey before the implementation of compensation and
site clearance, in order to compare the change in status before and after the impact of the project.
The household sample survey needs to ensure adequate representation of affected persons and
must include 10% of households affected and 100% of households severely affected.
508.   Through a graduated process of consolidations, analysis and assessment, a monthly progress
report will be send by the Regional Office to the Social Specialist at K1-PMO. The K1-PMO would
review these monthly reports and identify technical, managerial or regulatory and safeguard issues
with regards to the compliance of the ESIA/ESMP including LRRPs provisions. A corrective action
plan would be developed by the K1-PMO and debated internally to determine the appropriate
interventions. These interventions would be conveyed to the MoE Management through a Quarterly
report for approval and subsequently implemented by MoE PMO. The PMO would prepare a
quarterly progress report (QPR) with ESMP compliance status and Semi-annual monitoring report
and present it to the MoE and World Bank .

15 PATH TO PREPARE                                    THE   LIVELIHOOD    RESTORATION            AND
   RESETTLEMENT PLANS
15.1 RPs preparation
509.    As indicated above, two LRRPs will be prepared: i) the first one (LRRP1) for construction sites,
early works and associated facilities and ii) a second one later for the reservoir -impounded area
and water protection zone (LRRP2). Based on the LRRF, the consultants hired by the 1-PMO shall
prepare LRRPs including livelihood restoration activities for the Project and submit it to MoE for
review and approval. LRRP should be oriented to address specific issues raised by the project
(displacement, loss of livelihoods associated with specific loss of access to assets in some sectors
such as pastures and others).
510.   K1-PMO is responsible for the development of the LRRPS which will subsequently be
submitted to the WB for approval before there is the final approval by the MoE. K1-PMO staff is
responsible for this task in coordination with PAPs, government agencies at all levels, and local social
organizations to implement the detailed LRRP.
511.   The LRRP preparation requires community participation an analysis in all aspects to be
included in a social assessment and evaluation. The following procedures are implemented in the
planning phase of a Project.
15.2 Steps for LRRPs preparation
512.   Prepare ToR for LRRPs preparation. Based on the LRRF, SMEC, as part of their contract,
prepared ToR for the two LRRPs preparation. These ToRs are presented in Annex 5.
513.    Bidding and hiring process of LRRPs Consultant. Once the ToRs are completed, K1-PMO will
start the bidding and hiring process to select a Consultant in charge of LRRPs preparation.
514.    Inception Report. The selected consultant will prepare an inception report detailing the
methodology used to prepare LRRP1. This inception report will be submitted to K1-PMO and the
WB for approval. At the time of preparation of LRRP2, the consultant will prepare a new inception
report.
    1. Social Screening. The selected consultant shall update the social screening conducted in
       2025 to collect information on proposed land location, area, ownership details, current land
       use, tenure status of present land use and unit of government having jurisdiction on land
       etc. for both the construction site, the reservoir area and the WPZ.
515.    Establish and inform Cut-off Dates. Before the start of the census survey, the MoE will notify
the cut-off dates for i) construction site (RP1); ii) inundated area and WPZ (RP2). The cut-off date
will be the dates of the census survey for each LRRP . These dates shall be considered as the dates
for declaring affected persons eligible to receive entitlements. No persons who move into the
project area after the determination of the ‘Cut-off-date” will be eligible for any benefit. Appropriate
measures will be put in place to prevent informal settlers moving into the project area after the cut-
off dates.
516.     Census Survey. The census survey shall be carried out by K1-PMO with the involvement of a
consultant and local bodies using a structured questionnaire to record the details of the affected
persons. The exercise will help to: (i) prevent further influx of persons within the identified project
area; (ii) Assess the magnitude of impact to private assets and livelihoods; and (iii) Assess the extent
of physical and/or economic displacement. The census will be based on the preliminary design

  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                      Official Use Only   Page 140
                                                                                               of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


included in the feasibility study. Two census will be prepared; one for the LRRP1 and one for the
LRRP2.
517.     Socio Economic Survey. K1-PMO, with the assistance of a consultant, will conduct socio-
economic surveys among affected people out to establish baseline socio-economic status and living
standards which will become the basis for measuring the changes in the living standards during the
project implementation and end of the project implementation. The survey shall cover all impacted
project affected people in particular all pastures users and the survey shall also collect gender-
disaggregated data to address gender issues in resettlement. The socio-economic survey shall be
carried out using a structured questionnaire, that would capture details of the standard of living,
inventory of assets, sources of income, level of indebtedness, a profile of household members,
perceived benefits and impacts of the project and resettlement preferences for impacted
households likely to be displaced. This information along with the census survey data would
facilitate the preparation of LRRPs to mitigate adverse impact.
518.    Due Diligence Review of Early Works and Associated Facilities. The initial review of some
of the proposed interventions revealed that some development activities may be planned or on-
going in areas where the project will be implemented and which may considered to be associated
with the project per definition of “Associated Facility” in ESS1.8. Due diligence review report will be
prepared, as part of LRRP1 preparation, to assess if land acquisition conducted for these early works
and associated activities were in compliance with the principles of ESS5 and the regulations of the
Kyrgyz Republic. Correctives actions may be proposed to ensure such compliance.
519.    Replacement Costs Survey (RCS). As required by the World Bank’s ESS5 on Involuntary
Resettlement, RCS will need to be carried out to establish the basis for calculation of replacement
costs for all the lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs
to be completed to establish compensation rates for all LRRPs that are prepared under the Project.
MoE will hire an independent appraisal company (appraiser) to conduct RCS according to the
regulations and calculation of compensation will be carried out based on the Entitlement Matrix
approved as part of LRRF.
    2. Identification of new pastures. By order of the MoE, branches of the State Agency for Land
       Resources, Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography under the Cabinet of Ministers of the Kyrgyz
       Republic in Toktogul and Toguz-Toro districts will carry out cadastral, land management and
       topographic surveys to identify pasture plots on public land that could replace pastures lost.
520.    Consultations. Focus group discussions, key informant interviews, community consultations
with different impacted groups as well as other stakeholders will be conducted to ascertain their
concerns and views for the proposed project. Consultations with women and vulnerable group, in
particular, will be carried out to understand their specific concerns and views. Based on the outcome
of these consultations, if required, suitable mitigation measures will be incorporated into the project
and LRRPs. The Social Specialist, K1-PMO will also participate in the consultation meetings. The
consultation process will be in line with the SEP.
521.   Livelihood Restoration Program (LRP). As part of LRRP2 preparation, the LRRP prepared
under this LRRF will be updated following new consultations with communities and PAPs.
    Draft LRRP preparation. K1-PMO will hire a consultant to prepare the LRRPs depending on the
    outcome of socioeconomic surveys, census, ESIA and based on this LRRF. The LRRPs will also
    include entitlements for different type of impacts, socio economic characteristics of the affected
    persons, institutional mechanisms, implementation schedules, budgets, grievance redress


  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                   Official Use Only     Page 141
                                                                                              of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


    mechanism, coordination of implementation in conjunction with civil works procurement and
    construction schedules and monitoring mechanisms. The LRRPs will comply with the principles
    outlined in this LRRF. Outlines of the LRRPs is presented in Annex 5.
522. Process of LRRPs Review and project approval. The final draft of each LRRP signed by K1-
PMO management is sent to WB for review and then to MoE for approval
523.    LRRPs disclosure. All approved LRRPs within X days from the date of acceptance, will be
disclosed on MoE website, concerned Executive and Implementing Agencies’ offices, and the World
Bank’s portal prior to the initiations of construction work.
524.    In all the above processes K1-PMO would co-ordinate/oversee the process of securing land
including implementation of LRRPs, if applicable. K1-PMO would also ensure that the construction
will start only after the land has been transferred to respective Implementing Agencies and all
compensation and support are provided to eligible PAPs.
                             Table 54: Summary of Activities to be Conducted for each LRRP
              Activities                  LRRP1: Construction Site, Early   LRRP2: Reservoir Area and
                                         Works and Associated Facilities   Water Protection Zone (WPZ)
 525.   Prepare ToRs                 for SMEC to prepare ToRs for both LRRPs (See Annex 5)
    LRRPs preparation

    prepare LRRPs

15.3 Implementation of the LRRP
531.   Within X days from the date of approval of each of the LRRPs, K1-PMO will conduct the
following tasks:
       1. Negotiations. K1-PMO will develop draft agreements (redemption) regarding acquisition
          of land plots and other non-land assets for the Project, jointly with the branches of the
          State Agency for Land Resources, Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography under the Cabinet of
          Ministers of the Kyrgyz Republic in the Toktogul and Toguz-Toro districts and submit them
          to the PAP for consideration.
           532. Conclusion of agreements. K1-PMO will negotiate with the PAPs on the terms of land
           acquisition (based on independent valuator assessment of compensation rates) , payment
           of compensation and, if an agreement is reached, conclude an agreement on the
           permanent acquisition of a land plot or other non-land assets.
       2. Payment of compensation. Compensation is paid to the legitimate owner/user by transfer
          to the name (account) of the legitimate owner/user . If the bank account details are not
          specified, the funds are deposited in the name of the legitimate owner/user at the location
          of the acquired assets. The amount of compensation for the acquisition land and non-land
          assets owned by several persons on the basis of common ownership is determined in
          proportion to the shares in the common ownership of such property.
       3. State registration of transactions. Sends the agreement on the acquisition of a land plot
          and other non-land assets for registration to the authorized state body in the field of
          registration of rights to real estate in accordance with the legislation of the Kyrgyz Republic.
       4. Resettlement. K1-PMO, together with local government bodies and local self-government,
          organizes and resolves issues of relocation of legitimate owner/user and their families to
          new places (pastures) provided by decision of the aiyl okmotu.
       5. Refusal of the PAP to accept the land and/or non-land assets acquisition or the terms of
          the acquisitions. In case of disagreement of the PAP with the land acquisition and
          compensation process and its terms, the K1-PMO shall consider the complaint in
          accordance with Chapter 10: Grievances Redress Mechanism.
           533. Livelihood Restoration. K1-PMO and consultants will consult PAPs eligible to the
           LRRP and will present to them various suitable income restoration measures as described
           in Chapter 6. When eligible PAPs made their choice K1-PMO will prepare a contract
           agreement between K1-PMo and PAPs interested to participate in the LRRP.

  ANNEX 1: MINUTES OF PUBLIC MEETINGS (FIRST ROUND, OCTOBER NOVEMBER 2024)

1.1 National Consultations (Bishkek) of the Ecological and Social Study Technical Assistance for
Kambarata 1 Hydropower Plant Project Meeting Minutes
Date and Time                              : 19.11.2024
Organizer                                  : Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic
Location                                   : Bishkek, Kyrgyz Republic
TOPIC/OBJECTIVE
Conducting the Environmental and Social Assessment. Initial National Consultations.
The Purpose of the Consultation is letting all interested parties (governmental, non-governmental,
institutions, and non-profit organizations) ask questions, express their concerns, and provide
suggestions on the Project.
SUMMARY OF INFORMATION PRESENTED
The Consultants presented the Presentation and opened the Q&A session. The facilitator directed
raised questions to the responsible parties to answer. The Consultation included all project-related
aspects, including environmental and social, legal, technical, compensation, management, and
communication matters. Suggested proposals and feedback from participants were taken into
consideration. Some questions must be answered upon completing the survey/steps by the next
Consultation Session. The languages of conduct for the Consultation are English, Russian, and Kyrgyz.
Simultaneous translation was provided.
SUMMARY OF PARTICIPANTS
A total of 35 participants including 9 NGO representatives took part in the consultations. Females
accounted for 22% of the total participants. Participants also included local and international NGOs,
various Institutional groups, from local media, research educational bodies such as Association of
Women in Energy, environmental coalition, district level regulatory bodies (Toktogul district akim),
various ministries such as National Institute of Public Health of the Ministry of Health, Ministry of
Emergency Situations and different individual from epidemic background such as pollical scientist
etc.
Invitations were sent in advance via email and official letter from the Ministry of Energy, allowing
ample time for international NGOs to arrange their travel. Special invitations were also extended to
representatives of Civil Society to ensure their active participation.
Online participation was also organized for those interested stakeholders. The link to the event was
provided in advance. All necessary efforts were made to ensure that the consultations were
inclusive, taking into account the diverse interests and needs.

1.2 Local Consultations (Nichke-Say village, Toktogul district) of the Ecological and Social Study
Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes

Date and Time            : October 22, 2024 14:00

Organizer                : K1 HPP PMO, with support from SMEC

Location                 : Nichke-Say village, the former building of Uturov Z.N

TOPIC/OBJECTIVES
The objective of the meeting is to provide information on the goals and current activities of the
Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. According to the Kyrgyz Republic’s regulations and international
standards, a detailed Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) must be conducted to
assess and mitigation project’s risks and impacts, in addition to address specific concerns of local
communities. Consultations with stakeholders interested in the project are essential for gaining a
deeper understanding of their interests and concerns.
Concerns of local residents and communities will be considered seriously while carrying out the
ESIA. So the primary purpose of the meeting is to ensure transparency in project planning and
implementation.
SUMMARY OF INFORMATION PRESENTED
E.S. Mukhambetov, Head of the Department of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic,
presented on the Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. The main points discussed were as follows,
    • Presentation of the Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project.
    • Construction will be carried out with the support of the World Bank.
    • The planned implementation period is 6.5 years.
    • HPP capacity - 5 billion kWh.
    • Creation of 3,000 jobs with priority hiring of residents.
    • Average salary - 50,000 Soms.
    • Prepare infrastructure: concrete dam, new roads, bridges and substation.
    • The contractor is SMEC, an Australian company engaged in environmental and social
       assessment of the project.
SUMMARY OF PARTICIPANTS
A total of 44 participants took part in the consultations. Females accounted for 25% of the total
participants. Participants also included local authorities, community organizations, projects
affected people, including the vulnerable groups.
Invitations were sent through local government authorities, community organizations, as well as
WhatsApp Messenger. Meetings were held with Ayil Okmotu (Local authority) to inform and
engage participants, especially project affected people. Special invitations were extended to
project affected people to ensure their active participation.
All necessary efforts were made to ensure that the consultations were inclusive, taking into
account the diverse interests and needs.

Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydropower Plant Project Meeting Minutes

Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. According to the Kyrgyz Republic’s regulations and international
standards, a detailed Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) must be conducted to
assess and mitigation project’s risks and impacts, in addition to address specific concerns of local
communities. The ESIA will evaluate the project's potential impacts and propose mitigation
measures.

The Ministry of Energy and its potential international partners view consultations with
stakeholders interested in the project as essential for gaining a deeper understanding of their
interests and concerns.

Concerns of local residents and communities will be considered seriously while carrying out the
ESIA.

The primary purpose of the meeting is to ensure transparency in project planning and
implementation.

SUMMARY OF INFORMATION PRESENTED
The head of the Village Toluk provided a brief overview of previous meetings related to the
Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. Then, he highlighted the key issues: clarifying boundaries, assessing
flooded land, and discussing compensation.
A representative of the Ministry of Energy emphasized the importance of the Kambar-Ata-1 HPP
project as a national flagship and reported on $5 million in research funding from the World Bank.
The representative explained the project's impact on the lands of the Toluk, Nichke-Sai, and Sary-
Kamysh regions and reported on the role of international partners (Uzbekistan and Kazakhstan) in
the project. The representative also answered residents' questions regarding timing,
compensation, and environmental impacts.
The representative of SMEC company reported on SMEC's activities within the environmental and
social assessment. The World Bank standards in the projects were also outlined. The grievance
redress mechanism with local communities was presented.
SUMMARY OF PARTICIPANTS

A total of 67 participants took part in the consultations. Females accounted for 2,9% of the total
participants. Participants also included local authorities, community organizations, projects
affected people .

1.6 Local Consultations (Sary-Kamysh ayil aimak, Toktogul disctrict) of the Ecological and Social

Date and Time            : October 30, 2024 11:30-14:00

Organized                : K1 HPP PMO, with support from SMEC

Location                 : Sary Kamysh village, Sary Kamysh Aiyl Aimak, Toktogul district

TOPIC/OBJECTIVE
The objective of the meeting is to provide information on the goals and current activities of the
Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. According to the Kyrgyz Republic’s regulations and international
standards, a detailed Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) must be conducted to
assess and mitigation project’s risks and impacts, in addition to address specific concerns of local
communities.
Consultations with stakeholders interested in the project are essential for gaining a deeper
understanding of their interests and concerns.
Concerns of local residents and communities will be considered seriously while carrying out the
ESIA. The primary purpose of the meeting is to ensure transparency in project planning and
implementation.
SUMMARY OF INFORMATION PRESENTED

E.S. Mukhambetov, Head of the Department of the Ministry of Energy of the Kyrgyz Republic,
presented on the Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project. The main points of the report:
    • Presentation of the Kambar-Ata-1 HPP project.
    • Construction will be carried out with the support of the World Bank.
    • The planned implementation period is 6.5 years.
    • HPP capacity - 5 billion kWh.
    • Creation of 3,000 jobs with priority hiring of local residents.
    • Average salary - 50,000 soms.
    • Preparation of infrastructure: concrete dam, new roads, bridges and substation.
    • The contractor is SMEC, an Australian company engaged in environmental and social
       assessment of the project.
To improve the accuracy of the survey, maps of the flooded areas have been prepared. Residents
have asked that all objects be marked on them: bridges, trails, huts and other important objects
for the population.
SUMMARY OF PARTICIPANT
A total of 50 participants took part in the consultations. Females accounted for 20% of the total
participants. Participants also included local authorities, community organizations, projects

‘3.2 Local Consultations (Aral village, Toktogul district) on the results of the Ecological and Social
Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP
 Location                 Aral Village, Atai Ayil Aimak (including Kargalyk AA)
 Date                     6 October 2025
 Time                     11:00 am – 2:30 pm
 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                       Checked/Approved by        Zirgham Afridi
Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental
and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having
completed the environmental and social assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the
consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts, and proposed mitigation measures
with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible
and transparent manner, ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential
environmental and social impacts—such as land use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have
been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from
residents and representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA
and associated Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a
critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and implementation align with both national
regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and
inclusion, allowing community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future
stages of project development.
Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings
and impacts identified in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social
aspects, including potential impacts during construction and operation, and the corresponding
mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of
the Kyrgyz Republic had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and
English, along with a Kyrgyz language version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance
with national requirements and international standards, public notices and letters were
distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to inform
them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts
ahead of the consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the
sessions.
Summary of Participants
 Participants                               Details
 Residents of the Atai and                  • Head of the Atai Ayil Aimak
 Kargalyk Ayil Okmotus                      • Number of participants: 69 people including 23 men and 46 women.

‘3.3 Local Consultations (Nikche-Sai village, Toktogul district) on the results of the Ecological and
Social Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Nikche-Sai village, Imanalyievskii Ayil Aimak

 Date                     9 October 2025

 Time                     12:00 pm – 3:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                      Checked/Approved by      Zirgham Afridi, 12 Nov 2025


A-1            Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental
and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having
completed the environmental and social assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the
consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts, and proposed mitigation measures
with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible
and transparent manner, ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential
environmental and social impacts—such as land use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have
been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from
residents and representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA
and associated Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a
critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and implementation align with both national
regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and
inclusion, allowing community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future
stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings
and impacts identified in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social
aspects, including potential impacts during construction and operation, and the corresponding
mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of
the Kyrgyz Republic had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and
English, along with a Kyrgyz language version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance
with national requirements and international standards, public notices and letters were
distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to inform
them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts
ahead of the consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the
sessions.

A-2            Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental
and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having
completed the environmental and social assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the
consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts, and proposed mitigation measures
with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible
and transparent manner, ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential
environmental and social impacts—such as land use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have
been assessed and addressed.


  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                          Official Use Only       Page 203
                                                                                                       of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from
residents and representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA
and associated Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a
critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and implementation align with both national
regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and
inclusion, allowing community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future
stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings
and impacts identified in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social
aspects, including potential impacts during construction and operation, and the corresponding
mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of
the Kyrgyz Republic had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and
English, along with a Kyrgyz language version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance
with national requirements and international standards, public notices and letters were
distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to inform
them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts
ahead of the consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the
sessions.

‘3.5 Local Consultations (Toluk village (1st Meeting), Toktogul district) on the results of the Ecological and
Social Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project Meeting Minutes

 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Toluk village, Toluk Ayil Aimak

 Date                     8 October 2025

 Time                     11:00 am – 3:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]               Checked/Appr     Zirgham Afridi, 17 Nov 2025
                                                            oved by


A-3            Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental
and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having
completed the environmental and social assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the
consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts, and proposed mitigation measures
with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible
and transparent manner, ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential
environmental and social impacts—such as land use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have
been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from
residents and representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA
and associated Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a
critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and implementation align with both national
regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and
inclusion, allowing community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future
stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings
and impacts identified in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social
aspects, including potential impacts during construction and operation, and the corresponding
mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of
the Kyrgyz Republic had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and
English, along with a Kyrgyz language version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance
with national requirements and international standards, public notices and letters were
distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to inform
them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.
This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts
ahead of the consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the
sessions.

‘3.6: Local Consultations (Toluk village (2nd meeting), Toktogul district) on the results of the
Ecological and Social Study Technical Assistance for Kambarata 1 Hydro-power Plant Project
Meeting Minutes
 Meeting Name             Kambarata-1 HPP

 Location                 Toluk village, Toluk Ayil Aimak (2nd meeting)

 Date                     10 October 2025

 Time                     11:00 am – 2:00 pm

 Minutes by               [SMEC Contact Name]                      Checked/Approved by      Zirgham Afridi, 18 Nov 2025


A-4             Topic/Objective of Consultations
The purpose of the meetings was to present and discuss the findings of the Draft Environmental
and Social Impact Assessment (ESIA) for the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Project (K1 HPP). Having
completed the environmental and social assessment and prepared the full draft of the ESIA, the
consultation aimed to share the key results, identified impacts, and proposed mitigation measures
with affected communities and other local stakeholders.
The consultations were designed to inform participants about the ESIA findings in an accessible
and transparent manner, ensuring that community members clearly understood how potential
environmental and social impacts—such as land use, biodiversity, and livelihood changes—have
been assessed and addressed.
An equally important objective was to gather feedback, comments, and local knowledge from
residents and representatives of local authorities, which will be used to refine and finalize the ESIA
and associated Environmental and Social Management Plans (ESMPs). These discussions are a
critical step in ensuring that the project’s design and implementation align with both national
regulatory requirements and international best practice, including the World Bank’s
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF).
The consultations reinforce the project’s commitment to open communication, transparency, and
inclusion, allowing community perspectives to be reflected in the final documentation and future
stages of project development.

Summary of Information Presented
At the beginning of each meeting, a presentation was delivered summarizing the main findings
and impacts identified in the Draft ESIA. The presentation covered key environmental and social
aspects, including potential impacts during construction and operation, and the corresponding
mitigation and management measures proposed under the ESMPs.
Prior to the field consultations, the Project Management Office (PMO) of the Ministry of Energy of
the Kyrgyz Republic had formally disclosed the full ESIA report on its official website in Russian and
English, along with a Kyrgyz language version of the Non-Technical Summary (NTS). In accordance
with national requirements and international standards, public notices and letters were
distributed to affected communities at least 30 days in advance of the consultations to inform
them of the disclosure and the upcoming meetings.




  P509251-f2a98032-83c9-4178-a2dc-730e1e088412.docx                                Official Use Only       Page 230
                                                                                                             of 278
Kambarata-1 HPP


This approach ensured that participants were familiar with the project and its anticipated impacts
ahead of the consultations, enabling informed discussions and meaningful feedback during the
sessions.

                                                                  wind, restoring natural microclimatic functions. Floodplain areas near the reservoir will be monitored to prevent
                                                                  excessive flooding. A real-time meteorological monitoring system will be implemented to allow us to adjust water
