     ANNEX 5: Terms of Reference for Resettlement Plan Preparation for
                        Construction Site and Associated Facilities
1. Introduction and Background
The Government of the Kyrgyz Republic has prioritized the development of its hydropower
potential as a central pillar of national energy security and sustainable economic growth. Given the
country’s mountainous terrain and rich water resources, particularly from the Naryn River basin,
the hydropower sector plays a critical role in domestic energy supply and regional energy
cooperation.
As part of this national strategy, the Government, through the Ministry of Energy is seeking the
financing for development of the Kambarata-1 Hydropower Plant (K-1 HPP)—a major infrastructure
project that aligns with the objectives set out in the Sustainable Development Strategy (2018–2040)
and the National Development Program to 2026. Once operational, K-1 HPP is expected to be the
largest hydropower project in the Kyrgyz Republic and the broader Central Asia region, with an
installed capacity of approximately 1,860 MW and annual generation of about 5,640 GWh—
equivalent to nearly 50% of the country’s current installed capacity. K-1 HPP is expected to improve
the energy and food security of the Kyrgyz Republic while enhancing the country’s energy export
revenue through the distribution of surplus power to other Central Asian countries, including
Uzbekistan, Tajikistan and Pakistan. The large reservoir of K-1 HPP on the Naryn River is likely to
improve the operation of the Toktogul HPP reservoir, which can provide a much-needed balance to
the water management regime in the Naryn–Syr Darya Basin. The proposed project will also emerge
as crucial step in fulfilling the government’s vision for a green and affordable energy future.
The proposed site for the K-1 HPP is located in the middle reaches of the Naryn River, about 14.5
km upstream of the existing Kambarata-2 HPP dam, in the Toktogul District of Jalalabad Region.
Figure 1-1 shows the locations of the dam, HPP, and associated facilities.




                                                                                             Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP




Figure 1-1: Locations of the Dam, HPP, and Associated Facilities

The proposed Project consists of the following main elements:
     •     Roller-compacted concrete (RCC) gravity dam is 10 m wide at the crest and has a maximum height
           above the riverbed of 256 m.
     •     A reservoir area of 61 km2 at a full supply level (FSL) of 1,198 msl. The inundated area extends
           approximately 68 km upstream from the Dam wall.
     •     An overground powerhouse including Francis-type turbines with a total electricity generating capacity
           of 1,860 MW.
     •     The permanent resettlement of persons temporarily and permanently residing and pastures,
           structures, assets and sources of livelihood within the proposed inundation area. Also, restoration of
           access and social infrastructure affected.
     •     The construction of temporary and permanent access roads and bridge structures within the Dam
           site.
     •     The construction of water pipelines and tunnels.
     •     Quarry sites to source raw materials for the Dam.
     •     Temporary concrete batching plant, materials storage, waste disposal, construction sites and
           workforce accommodation facilities.
     •     Permanent and temporary accommodation facilities for Dam and hydropower operations and
           maintenance personnel.
     •     Associated facilities (i.e. a 5.6 km access road the K-1 site to the existing road network; a bridge over
           the Naryn River; temporary work camp; a 23.6 km long 110kv overhead transmission line; and a
           110/6 kv substation).
As part of the Project preparation, the Ministry of Energy, through its Project Management Office
(PMO), has engaged SMEC to undertake a comprehensive Environmental and Social Impact
Assessment (ESIA). This assessment has been conducted in accordance with the World Bank’s


                                                                                                            Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
Environmental and Social Framework (ESF) and relevant national legislation. In line with the
requirements of Environmental and Social Standard 5 (ESS5) – Land Acquisition, Restrictions on
Land Use, and Involuntary Resettlement – a Resettlement and Livelihood Restoration Framework
(RLRF) has also been developed for submission to the World Bank for review and approval. Two
Resettlement Plans (RPs) will be prepared under this framework:
RP1 – covering land acquisition for construction site and associated facilities;
RP2 – to address impacts related to the reservoir impoundment area and the water protection zone (WPZ).
This Term of Reference (TOR) has been developed for the RP1 preparation.

2. Preliminary Identification of Land Acquisition and Resettlement Impacts
   due to Construction Site and Associated Facilities
The following sections present a summary of the findings from the ESIA conducted by SMEC in 2025,
specifically focusing on potential impacts related to land acquisition and resettlement due to
construction site and construction of associated facilities.

2.1. Potential Impacts due to Main Construction Site
The construction site is located in an area with no human activities due to the steep slopes and the
semi-desert vegetation. The area needed for the main construction site is estimated at 34.45 ha
affecting two Aiyl Aimak (AAs): Toluk and E. Imanaliev. At the dam site, the land is barren public
land. There are no pastures, and no structures located at this site.
For auxiliary works, according to the Interim Feasibility Study Report provided by AFRY as of January
2025, potential sites for auxiliary works—including the crushing plant, workshop, work camp, and
quarry site—have been identified. These components are expected to require approximately
113.93 hectares of land, primarily located in Toluk and Imanaliev AAs.
All identified land is believed to be unused public land, with some small pasture areas interspersed.
Number of affected people in these areas remains undetermined at the time of preparing the ESIA
report. However, given the local pasture use practices, it is expected that those utilizing this land
will be accounted for in the total number of pasture users affected by the reservoir area.
It should be noted that the final selection of sites has not yet been determined, and it remains
unclear whether all identified locations will be used. As a result, the total area of affected land may
change significantly once final decisions are made. Additionally, it is still unknown whether these
areas will be temporarily or permanently acquired from the local community, pending further
clarification at the later Project stage.
The construction of the dam and other works will require a large number of workers during 10
years with a peak of 3,000 workers. Most the workers will be migrant workers. At the time of the
ESIA report preparation, the final location of the workers’ camp had not yet been determined.
Possible locations include: (i) Ketmen Tobo Village; (ii) an affected village (Nichke-Sai); or iii) the
dam site.

2.2. Potential Impacts due to Construction of Associated Facilities
A number of associated facilities have been identified, including access road, a bridge over the
Naryn River, transportation tunnel, 110kV overhead transmission line towers and substation and
other components (e.g., Water Tank, Treatment Plant, General Service Facilities, etc) (Table 2.2-1).
It is estimated that 30.35 ha of land will be acquired for these associated facilities. The affected
areas include 11.67 ha of pasture and 18.68 ha of other public land (water, shrub, etc.). As part of
this RP, a Due Diligence Report (DDR) will be prepared for these associated facilities to ensure that



                                                                                                  Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
land acquisition and resettlement, if any, was conducted in compliance with the proposed project
policy..

3. Objectives of Consultancy Services
The task required is to prepare a Resettlement Plan (RP) for the construction site and associated
facilities of the K1-HPP Project. The RP preparation must be compliant with the RLRF of the Project,
World Bank’s ESF and the Kyrgyz Republic’s relevant laws and regulations. The document will be
prepared to meet the following objectives of ESS5.
To avoid involuntary resettlement or, when unavoidable, minimize involuntary resettlement by exploring
    project design alternatives.
To avoid forced eviction.
To mitigate unavoidable adverse social and economic impacts from land acquisition or restrictions on land use
by: (a) providing timely compensation for loss of assets at replacement cost6 and (b) assisting displaced
persons in their efforts to improve, or at least restore, their livelihoods and living standards, in real terms, to
pre-displacement levels or to levels prevailing prior to the beginning of project implementation, whichever is
higher.
To improve living conditions of poor or vulnerable persons who are physically displaced, through provision of
adequate housing, access to services and facilities, and security of tenure.
To conceive and execute resettlement activities as sustainable development programs, providing sufficient
investment resources to enable displaced persons to benefit directly from the Project, as the nature of the
Project may warrant.
 To ensure that resettlement activities are planned and implemented with appropriate disclosure of
information, meaningful consultation, and the informed participation of those affected.
To ensure no legacy issues remain with past land acquisition.
As part of the RP, due diligence of the land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement activities
carried out for the associated facilities of the Project will be conducted. The assessment aims to:
Determine the extent to which land acquisition and resettlement activities were conducted in alignment with
the principles and requirements of ESS5, particularly regarding voluntary or involuntary resettlement,
compensation at replacement cost, livelihood restoration, and grievance redress mechanisms.
Identify any gaps between the land acquisition/resettlement practices applied by the implementing agency or
third parties and the World Bank’s ESS5, and propose corrective actions where necessary to ensure
compliance with the ESF and the RLPF of the Project.
Assess whether affected persons have been adequately informed, consulted, compensated, and assisted, with
attention to vulnerable groups and gender considerations.
Recommend corrective actions to address all the identified non-compliance or residual risks to ensure the
compliance with the World Bank’s ESF, ESS5, and the RLPF of the Project.

4. Scope of Works
The Consultant’s tasks shall include, but not be limited to, the following:
Prepare an inception report detailing the methodology used to prepare the RP. This inception report will be
submitted to K1-PMO and the WB for approval.




                                                                                                          Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
Update the social screening conducted in 2025 the Project, covering the rapid preliminary assessment to
collect information on proposed land location, area, ownership details, current land use, tenure status of
present land use and unit of government having jurisdiction on land, etc.
Carry out a census survey of all the people affected by the construction site and associated facilities using a
structured questionnaire (if any) if the updated social screening indicates that local residents or communities
will be affected due to land acquisition, access restrictions, or asset loss.
Prepare an inventory of loss (IOL) based on the final design. This IOL will cover all impacts and asset losses.
It will develop a database of physical quantities of impacts and lay down the basis for developing an
entitlement policy and compensation package
Conduct a socio-economic survey (SES) to establish baseline data for use in the description of PAPs, provide a
basis for the design of, and budgeting for, the resettlement program, and inform baseline for monitoring and
evaluation of land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement of the Project.
Conduct due diligence review to assess if land acquisition conducted for these associated activities were in
compliance with the principles of ESS5 and the regulations of the Kyrgyz Republic. Correctives actions may be
proposed to ensure such compliance.
Conduct a Replacement Costs Survey (RCS) on affected land and non-land assets (if any). As required by the
World Bank’s ESS5, the RCS will need to be carried out to establish the basis for calculation of replacement
costs for all the lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs to be
completed to establish compensation rates for this RP. The consultant will calculate the cost of
compensation, assistance, and resettlement based on the RCS results and the Entitlement Matrix approved as
part of RLRF.
Conduct consultations with PAPs, local authorities, Non-government Organizations (NGOs) and relevant
stakeholder through public consultation meetings, focus group discussions (FGDs), key-informant interviews
(KIIs), and in-depth interviews to ascertain their opinions, concerns about various aspects of land acquisition,
in particular entitlements on compensation, assistance, and resettlement, replacement pasture, restoration of
loss of access to pastureland and livelihood restoration. Take the opinions and concerns into account and
ensure they are addressed and incorporated into the RP.
Consultations with women and vulnerable group, in particular, will be carried out to understand their specific
concerns and views. Based on the outcome of these consultations, if required, suitable mitigation measures
will be incorporated into the Project and RP.
Prepare a RP for construction site and associated facilities based on the outcome of the census and inventory
of losses, SES, RCS, due diligence findings, ESIA and the RLRF. The RP will also include entitlements for
different types of impacts, socio economic characteristics of the affected persons, corrective actions for land
acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement for associated facilities, institutional mechanisms,
implementation schedules, budgets, grievance redress mechanism, coordination of implementation in
conjunction with civil works procurement and construction schedules and monitoring mechanisms. The RP will
comply with the principles outlined in the RLRF. The outline of the RP is attached in Appendix 1.

5. Specific Tasks
5.1. Census Survey and Inventory of Losses (IOL)

The census survey and IOL shall be carried out for 100% of the affected households using a
structured questionnaire to record the details of the affected persons. The exercise will help to: (i)
prevent further influx of persons within the identified project area; (ii) Assess the magnitude of
impact to private assets and livelihoods; and (iii) Assess the extent of physical and/or economic
displacement. The census and IOL will be based on the preliminary design included in the feasibility
study.
The consultant is asked to identify the persons who will be affected by the Project, and establish an
inventory of land and assets to be affected following the steps below:
Develop a structured questionnaire for review and approval by K1-PMO and World Bank.




                                                                                                        Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
Approach the Municipal Enterprises and those in charge of land management who holds the land records to
collect (or purchase) of cadastral maps/land use maps on the project villages and AAs.
Overlay the map of the construction site and associated facilities on the land use maps of the relevant AAs.
This method will provide basic information such as types of affected lands; amounts of affected lands;
number of the plots, etc. The consultant will review of cadastral records together with the Municipal
Enterprises and land management officers and village and AA leaders.
Lay-out the area required for construction site and associated facilities on the ground with support of a design
engineer, representatives from Municipal Enterprises, village leaders/AA leaders and GPS, the consultant will
identify the location of the Project area in the field and identify the impacts due to construction site
preparation and construction of associated facilities;
Together with village leaders and Municipal Enterprises of affected AAs to identify the affected households
and conduct interviews with household heads or their spouses using the questionnaire to determine their
scope of land acquisition impacts.
Take photos of affected households (the heads of household - husband and wife - or with many household
members as possible) with their household ID in front of their affected house/land. All the affected land and
assets should be photographed along with GIS coordinates.
Analyse the data on the land acquisition impacts.
The following data and information need to be collected during the census, but not limited to:
(i) Affected assets that need to be enumerated for each project component;
Private land (agricultural land, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or with access affected or
restriction on use: affected area, land ownership, current land use, total area of landholding for each affected
land type, number of land owners/land users, number of PAPs.
Public land (pastureland, game hunting grounds, etc.) that will be permanently acquired for and/or with
access affected or restriction on use: affected area, total area of all pasture land used by each affected
household (AH) within and outside the Project area and current land use, type of affected pasture (e.g.,
summer, winter, spring and autumn), status of contract with Municipal enterprises or shepherds, quantity of
livestock grazing within the affected land, number of affected land users and the number of their family
members.
Contracts with government agencies for the use of biological resources of the lands, number of wild animals,
collected plants, number of users of biological resources.
Trees and long-term crops: quantity and type of affected crop/tree, use of crops/tree (e.g., fruits, trees) for
commercial sale, household consumption or any other purposes, number of affected households and
individuals.
Houses and other fixed structures upon land (houses, huts, sheepfolds, sheds, barns, fences, and trough
pens, etc.): quantity of affected structures, affected area, type of structure, construction materials of roof,
wall, floor, current use, structure ownership, number of structure users, number of physically displaced
households . Determine the impact extent (partially affected, fully affected or partially affected but the
remaining portion of the structure is no longer viable for continued use as its original function).
Public or community structures (roads, bridges, irrigation water system, etc.): dimensions of affected
structures, owners of affected structures, extent of impacts on access of local communities, etc.
Cultural assets (graves, burial sites, etc.): quantity of affected graves, grave ownership, names and cultural or
spiritual significance of burial sites and other cultural assets to local communities, implications for local
customs, practices, and identity.
Sources of income and livelihood: main source of household income/livelihood, average income, quantity of
affected livestock, etc.
(ii) For AHs who are shepherds that have income/livelihood affected, the following information to-
     be collected:
Number of years working as a shepherd;
Types of livestock managed (sheep, goats, cattle, yaks, etc.)
Number of livestock under their care



                                                                                                          Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
Seasonal patterns (e.g., year-round, seasonal herding)
Type of pastures used (summer, spring, winter)
Monthly/seasonal income from shepherding
Whether shepherding is their primary source of income
Other income-generating activities (if any)
Estimated income loss due to loss of pasture or job displacement
Access to grazing routes and natural resources (water, wood, etc.)
(iii) Vulnerable PAPs need to be enumerated which include the followings. Total number of people
      living in each AH should be listed.
Low-income households
Households headed by female with dependents;
Households headed by elderly person with no means of support;
Households having people with disabilities; and
Other vulnerable households (if any)
(iv) Preferences of AHs for compensation, assistance, and resettlement and livelihood restoration.
(v) Other land users. A hunting farm is an organization that has territory secured on a long-term
    lease basis, where sport and foreign hunting is conducted and a range of hunting and
    biotechnical measures are carried out aimed at protecting and reproducing the population of
    game animals and maintaining their numbers at an optimal level or not exceeding the
    ecological capacity of the land.
Hunting grounds are land and forest areas, mountain ranges, water areas and swamps that serve or can
    serve as habitat for wild animals, regardless of the ownership of these territories.
Mapping materials are cartographic materials containing detailed characteristics of forests and hunting
    grounds, varying in scale, topographic and special load depending on their intended purpose.
Registration of wildlife (animals, birds, fish)
Capital investments in biotechnical measures for the reproduction and protection of biological resources.

5.2. Socio-economic Survey
The SES will be carried out to establish baseline socio-economic status and living standards which
will become the basis for measuring the changes in the living standards during the Project
implementation and end of the Project implementation. The survey shall cover all impacted project
affected people in particular all pastures users and the survey shall also collect gender-
disaggregated data to address gender issues in resettlement. Depending on the results of the
census and inventory of losses, the survey size can be re-determined in consultation with the PMO
and World Bank before the SES is conducted. However, it is required the survey cover at minimum :
100% of winter pasture users and 50% of other pasture users;
100% of households with loss of structures; and
100% of vulnerable AHs.
Detailed tasks of the SES include:
Design survey instruments.
Organize trainings for survey team.
Sampling and selection of households: From the lists of affected households generated from the census and
inventory of losses to select households to be surveyed. Ensure representation across locations and impact
categories.



                                                                                                      Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
Conduct of household survey: carry out face-to-face interviews using structured questionnaires; ensure
informed consent and privacy of respondents and collect GPS coordinates and take photographs (with
permission) where necessary to validate locations and conditions.
Data entering, processing and analysing using Excel, SPSS, or other suitable software.
The SES shall be carried out using a structured questionnaire, that would capture details of the
following aspects
A profile of household members (full name, gender, age, marital status, highest educational attainment, main
and secondary occupations, monthly income);
Economic activities: average monthly household income and expenditures, savings and debt status, livestock,
pasture use, and farming practices;
Pasture management;
Standard of living: housing type and ownership, primary and secondary sources of fuel, drinking water, and
electricity for cooking and heating; toilet facilities.
Availability and accessibility to public infrastructure;
Social aid and government support;
Perceived benefits and impacts of the Project; and
Skills, training, and resources required by AHs to restore or improve their livelihoods.

5.3. Due Diligence Review on the land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement
     activities implemented for the associated facilities
A Due Diligence Report (DDR) will be prepared for these associated facilities. The objectives of the
Due Diligence Review are the following:
     Evaluate if all involuntary resettlement activities associated with the Associated Facilities were
     carried out in full compliance with regulations of Kyrgyz Republic.
     Confirm if the compensation payment/provision of support/resettlement done by local
     government (including its resettlement outcome) meets the objectives ESS5,
     Check if there are any resettlement related issues that remain pending at the time of Bank’s due
     diligence;
     Ensure that there is no reputational risk for the Bank regarding resettlement for this project


The consultant will undertake the following key tasks:
Review documents related to land acquisition, compensation, assistance, and resettlement activities
undertaken for the associated facilities.
Conduct site visits and public consultations with affected people, relevant agencies to collect quantitative and
qualitative information for assessing the performance and effectiveness of the land acquisition, compensation,
assistance, and resettlement and satisfaction of the affected people with the resettlement process.
Assess the compliance of compensation, assistance, and resettlement implemented for the associated facilities
with national legislation and objectives and requirements of the ESS5.
Identify discrepancies between the implemented compensation, assistance, and resettlement and
requirements of national laws and regulations as well as the ESS5.
Discuss the identified gaps or non-compliance issues with the K1-PMO and relevant agencies.
Provide recommendations for corrective actions to address identified gaps or non-compliance issues, including
preparation of a Corrective Action Plan with timelines, responsibilities, and budget.




                                                                                                       Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
5.4. Replacement Cost Survey
Following the results of the Inventory of Losses for the land acquisition for construction site and
associated facilities, the consultant will carry out a Replacement Cost Survey (RCS) for potentially
affected land and non-land assets in accordance with national regulations and full replacement cost
principles of World Bank policies. The RCS is to establish the basis for calculation of replacement
costs for all the lands/crops/structures/assets affected by the Project. In relation to this, RCS needs
to be completed to establish compensation rates for the RP that is prepared under the Project.
Based on the RCS results, calculation of compensation will be carried out based on the Entitlement
Matrix approved as part of RLRF.
Land: Conduct interviews with Representatives from the relevant agencies (e.g., Aiyl Okmotu of
    affected AAs, District level cadastral unit branches of the State Agency of Land Resources,
    Cadastre, Geodesy and Cartography), affected and unaffected landowners in the Project area to
    collect information on:
Recent market transactions and informal sales of land use rights.
Willingness-to-sell prices of both affected and unaffected households.
Associated transaction costs (e.g., administrative charges, registration or title fees, reasonable moving
    expenses, and any similar costs imposed on affected persons).
(i) Crops and Trees: Interview affected households, farmers, and local agricultural officers to
    assess:
For crops: The market prices for different types of perennial and annual crops over the past three years, crop
     yield per hectare.
For fruit or productive trees: cost of seedlings, time required for seedlings to reach maturity by species,
     average yield/value of mature trees per year and market prices of output (fruits, nuts, etc.) or prices at
     which tree owners are willing to sell their produce.
For timber trees: timber volume, and quality of each type of affected trees (species, diameter, height, age,
     and condition; current market price per cubic meter of timber.
(ii) Structures: Interview representatives of District Departments of Urban Planning and
     Architecture of the State Agency for Architecture, Construction, and Housing and Communal
     Services under the Cabinet of Ministers of the Kyrgyz Republic), affected households, local
     builders, and construction firms to determine:
Average construction costs per type of structure,
Labor and transportation costs,
Expenses related to obtaining building permits and registrations, if applicable.
(iii) Other cost and allowance: Interview local residents to determine
Cost of excavation, relocation, reburial and other related costs
Transportation costs for movable assets, including salvaged materials from original structures
(iv) Price Comparison and Validation:
Compare estimated replacement costs with the unit rates approved by the State Agency for Architecture,
   Construction, and Housing and Communal Services or other relevant bodies, if available.
Consult with district- and AA-level authorities to verify and validate findings.
(v) Cost Estimation and Reporting:
Propose unit rates for compensation of affected assets (land, structures, perennial and annual crops) based
    on replacement cost principles and without depreciation in consultation with PMO and World Bank;
Calculate the cost of compensation, assistance, and resettlement.




                                                                                                        Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
5.5. Public Consultations
    The consultant is required to conduct the following activities:
Carrying out a series of public consultation meetings including one consultative meeting with local authorities
     and relevant agencies at district and AA levels and one meeting with potentially affected households in
     each AA before the commencement of the census, inventory of losses, SES, and RCS.
    The Project information to be shared and consulted with potentially affected people and communities
    includes, but not limited to:

    • Project description and expected benefits of the Project;
    • Potential land acquisition and resettlement impacts due to the construction site and
       associated facilities;
    • Feasible measures to minimize and mitigate the land acquisition and resettlement impacts;
    • Proposed eligibility and entitlements for PAPs;
    • Availability of replacement land;
    • Restoration of loss of access to pasture land;
    • Needs of PAPs in livelihood restoration and relocation preference;
    • Schedules for the census, SES, and replacement cost survey;
    • Mechanisms for continuing meaningful consultation with and participation of PAPs,
       community, and other stakeholders in land acquisition and resettlement planning,
       implementation, and monitoring; and
    • Grievance redress mechanism.
Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities after completion of the census, inventory
of losses, SES, and RCS to present survey results, announced the cut-off date for eligibility for compensation,
assistance, and resettlement, and discussed the proposed entitlements with PAPs and communities.
Organizing public consultation meetings with PAPs and local authorities on the provisions of the draft RP before
submission to World Bank for review and approval.
Conducting in-depth interviews with key-informants (e.g., leaders of AA, village heads, Municipal Enterprises,
District Agriculture Management, Department of Pastures and Breeding Livestock, Women’s Union) to obtain
their insights about the project’s impacts on local residents and LRP (if any).
Organizing FGDs with specific groups of PAPs (e.g., vulnerable households, affected non-timber forest product
collectors, affected women) to understand their unique concerns, vulnerabilities, and recommendations.
These consultation activities should be held at a suitable time and place for women, and should also
take into account the needs of persons with disabilities (if any), as well as any barriers faced by socially
vulnerable groups, should also be considered when organizing such events. Whenever possible,
meetings should be held in neutral, accessible public spaces or within women-led civil society
organizations, where available.
All presentations must be delivered in the Kyrgyz language, and Project Information Booklets should
be distributed to all participants. All the concerns, suggestions, and recommendations raised by
meeting participants must be recorded and documented. This includes compiling attendance sheets
and photographic evidence of the consultations.

5.6. Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM)
The grievance redress mechanism (GRM) shall be developed in accordance with the WB’s ESS1 and
ESS10, the Project’s Stakeholder Engagement Plan (SEP) and the RLFR . In particular, the GRM will
be developed based on current ongoing GRM practices that have been applied locally as per



                                                                                                        Official Use Only
Kambarata-1 HPP
national laws and regulations and their design takes into account the views of affected communities
expressed during the RP preparation. Particular attention will be given to ensuring the GRM is
accessible, inclusive, and responsive, with specific provisions to facilitate access for disadvantaged
and vulnerable individuals or groups.

5.7. Special Considerations for the Needs of Women
All transactions related to physical or economic displacement require particular attention to gender.
For example:
Intra-household analysis may be needed where women’s and men’s livelihoods are affected differently.
Women’s and men’s preferences in terms of compensation mechanisms, such as replacement land or
   alternative access to natural resources rather than in cash, should be explored
Documentation of ownership or occupancy and compensation payments should be issued in the name of both
    spouses or single female heads of households
Proposed livelihood restoration measures, such as skills training, job opportunities etc., should be equally
    available to women and adapted to their needs
The consultation process should ensure that women’s perspectives are obtained, and their interests factored
    in.

6. Deliverables and Timeframe
The consultant shall submit the following reports:
Inception Report: This report will present the proposed methodology, resources, tools, and detailed schedule
    for delivering the assignment’s objectives and scope of work. It will include a detailed outline of the RP
    structure, in accordance with the Project's RLRF and the World Bank’s ESS5. Additionally, it also includes
    the update of the screening report will be also included in the Inception Report. The Inception Report shall
    be submitted to the K1-PMO and the World Bank for approval within one (1) week of contract signing.
Draft RP: This report will cover the full scope of work outlined in the TOR and will be prepared following
    comprehensive stakeholder engagement and consultation. The draft RP will be submitted to K1-PMO and
    the World Bank for review within nine (9) weeks of contract signing.
Final RP: This report will incorporate feedback from the Client, stakeholders, and the World Bank, ensuring all
    review comments are addressed and will be submitted within eleven (11) weeks of contract signing.

7. Qualification and Experience of the Consultant
The consulting firm must demonstrate substantial experience and technical capacity in the
preparation of Resettlement Plans, or other land acquisition and resettlement-related documents in
accordance with international standards, particularly the World Bank’s ESF and ESS5. The firm should
have at least seven (7) years of proven experience in implementing or supporting involuntary
resettlement and livelihood restoration activities in infrastructure, energy, or similar sectors,
preferably for projects financed by multilateral development banks such as the World Bank, ADB, or
EBRD. The firm must demonstrate a track record of effectively conducting socio-economic surveys,
meaningful consultations with affected persons (including vulnerable groups), and stakeholder
engagement in compliance with the principles of transparency, inclusiveness, and free, prior, and
informed participation. Familiarity with the national legal and institutional framework for land
acquisition and resettlement in the Kyrgyz Republic is highly desirable. The firm must also
demonstrate the ability to coordinate with government agencies, manage multidisciplinary teams,
and deliver high-quality, timely reports.
The consultant shall provide a multidisciplinary team with qualifications and experience as follows:

    associated facilities, and other project-affected areas.
